<div id="review_1304533986" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1304533986" />
    <a title="Jilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly"><img alt="Jilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435955932p2/25894509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1304533986?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jilly" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly">Jilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1304533986" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12687164925220198549">You know the expression "Jumping the Shark" for a television show that has been on too long and gotten horrible? Well, this book series has definitely been to Sea World on a motorcycle. <br/><br/><a href='http://photobucket.com/images/jump%20the%20shark' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434056812ra/15171861.gif' alt='jump the shark photo: Jump jumpz.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><i>I hope he had this book in his hand...</i><br/><br/>And, although I can be quite a masochist when it comes to finishing a series that I've started, I'm officially done.<br/><br/><a href='http://photobucket.com/images/throw%20book' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434056812ra/15171862.gif' alt='throw book photo: book2_zps29c02695.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><i>take that, people who told Charlaine Harris to keep writing when she was obviously out of ideas!</i><br/><br/>Sookie has actually managed to become even more unlikabl</span>
  <span id="freeText12687164925220198549" style="display:none">You know the expression "Jumping the Shark" for a television show that has been on too long and gotten horrible? Well, this book series has definitely been to Sea World on a motorcycle. <br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/jump%20the%20shark" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434056812ra/15171861.gif" alt="jump the shark photo: Jump jumpz.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>I hope he had this book in his hand...</i><br><br>And, although I can be quite a masochist when it comes to finishing a series that I've started, I'm officially done.<br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/throw%20book" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434056812ra/15171862.gif" alt="throw book photo: book2_zps29c02695.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>take that, people who told Charlaine Harris to keep writing when she was obviously out of ideas!</i><br><br>Sookie has actually managed to become even more unlikable in this book. I didn't think that was possible, and yet, here it is. I mean, we already knew she was stupid. Even she admits it.<br><br><b>
  <i>Okay, I've been stupid in the past. Not consistently stupid, but occasionally stupid.</i>
</b><br><br>Uh, no Sookie, you have been consistently stupid.<br><br>Plus, she is vain, selfish, and delusional. But, she did do one thing right and that was to get together with Eric. Unfortunately for Eric, though, is that she is a really crappy girlfriend. She is rude, argumentative, never understanding or compassionate, and rash. She breaks their blood bond without even talking to him first. It is like the equivalent of going to Mexico for a quickie divorce from your husband and then wondering why his feelings are hurt.<br><br><b>
  <i>I should have called Eric and warned him what was about to happen. But I'd been afraid he'd talk me out of it...</i>
</b><br><br>Oh, okay then. If you want to do something that you know that your spouse would absolutely be against, just do it behind their back.<br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/heads%20up" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434056812ra/15171863.gif" alt="heads up photo: Heads up! headball.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>Oops, sorry about that. I guess a little "heads up" would have been nice.</i><br><br>So, even though I waited forever for Sookie and Eric to finally get together, I have to say that I now think that Eric can do a lot better.<br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/tru%20blood%20eric" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_169830478" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/169830478" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/169830478?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101514382" href="/book/show/10424719-dead-reckoning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer169830478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4194942444330720401">It’s going to be difficult to write this review, because even though I finished reading this book this morning, I am having a hard time remembering what it was even about. I didn’t think that it was absolutely horrific, but I was <i>very</i> far from loving it. I read along slowly and with a mild interest, and then it was over. It was very forgettable.<br/><br/>So…there’s a fire-bombing at Merlotte’s, and some other stuff that apparently was perpetrated by one of Sookie’s random enemies from her past that I care</span>
  <span id="freeText4194942444330720401" style="display:none">It’s going to be difficult to write this review, because even though I finished reading this book this morning, I am having a hard time remembering what it was even about. I didn’t think that it was absolutely horrific, but I was <i>very</i> far from loving it. I read along slowly and with a mild interest, and then it was over. It was very forgettable.<br /><br />So…there’s a fire-bombing at Merlotte’s, and some other stuff that apparently was perpetrated by one of Sookie’s random enemies from her past that I care absolutely nothing about (why was that whole plot line even necessary?). Aaaaand, the new vampire big wig is being a royal pain, and there’s some stuff with the faeries and Sookie’s grandma …Bill is a sad sack hanger-on, and Amelia and Alcide make brief appearances to be total jerks and then leave. And then there’s roughly a combined one hundred pages or so of filler about Sookie cleaning her house, being a good hostess, waitressing, agonizing over morals, hosting baby showers, baking cheesy sticks, and apparently being in love with Sam all of a sudden. <br /><br />I used to enjoy all of those little details about Sookie – she’s the good ol’ girl with a big ol’ heart that I love to hang out with. But it all seemed to be washed out and repetitive and old in this book. I didn’t feel like I was hanging out with the real Sookie. It was like her character had suddenly been re-cast with a much older, less charismatic actress.<br /><br />The thing is, I am a huge fan of characters evolving and changing over time. In fact, I think that it’s absolutely essential in a series as long as this one. The opposite is the now dreadful (to me) hermetically sealed world of Stephanie Plum, where characters are not allowed to advance in any way. But, there’s gotta be a better way to reach your endgame than by throwing your characters of a cliff like so much garbage. I mean, the way that Eric is neatly excised from Sookie’s life (a few jam jars, some yarn, and a signed document and hey presto!) is just callous, given the amount of history and affection that we the readers have developed with him.<br /><br />So, I think that this might be the end for me and Sookie. But, I have a prediction - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[who wants to bet me that she uses the c.d. to save Sam in some way? <i>How could I not have known that I LOOOVED you all along?!!! Booo-hoooo….</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I’m probably wrong, but I look forward to reading the future reviews (which are likely to be much more entertaining that the future novels) to find out.<br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br />Rascal Flatts – <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=2MTSBcvI9DI" rel="nofollow noopener">These Days</a><br /> <br />I just want to take a minute to say thank you for generic leather ebook cases, and car windows that close. If not for you, I wouldn’t be able to read dozens, nay <i>hundreds</i> of embarrassing books without anyone being the wiser, or sing at the top of my lungs to music that I wouldn’t own up to liking in public (shhh, internet…don’t tell anyone!). I doubt this can even classify as “real” country music, which makes my love of Rascal Flatts even more pathetic. This song is my tribute to the Sookie, Eric, Amelia, Alcide, and Bill that I used to know. <i>Someone told me, after college, you all lost your personalities and became puppets. Wow, that ain't the folks I knew.</i> I’ll be checking my messages and dreaming of you, just in case you decide to come back.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4194942444330720401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_247041985" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/247041985" />
    <a title="Richard Derus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3920693-richard-derus"><img alt="Richard Derus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494992210p2/3920693.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/247041985?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard Derus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard Derus" href="/user/show/3920693-richard-derus">Richard Derus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780441020317" href="/book/show/9640019-dead-reckoning">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer247041985" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13027048693711963884">Rating: 3.8* of five<br/><br/><b>The Publisher Says</b>: There's a reckoning on the way ...<br/><br/>Sookie Stackhouse is a cocktail waitress in Bon Temps, Louisiana. It's a job which has its own challenges, but now the vampires and the shapeshifters are finally 'out', you'd think the supernaturals would get on with each other. But nothing is that simple in Bon Temps!<br/><br/>... and Sookie has a knack for being in trouble's way; not least when she witnesses the firebombing of Merlotte's, the bar where she works. Since Sam Merlott</span>
  <span id="freeText13027048693711963884" style="display:none">Rating: 3.8* of five<br><br><b>The Publisher Says</b>: There's a reckoning on the way ...<br><br>Sookie Stackhouse is a cocktail waitress in Bon Temps, Louisiana. It's a job which has its own challenges, but now the vampires and the shapeshifters are finally 'out', you'd think the supernaturals would get on with each other. But nothing is that simple in Bon Temps!<br><br>... and Sookie has a knack for being in trouble's way; not least when she witnesses the firebombing of Merlotte's, the bar where she works. Since Sam Merlotte is known to be two-natured, suspicion falls immediately on the anti-shifters in the area. Sookie suspects otherwise, but before she can investigate something else - something even more dangerous - comes up.<br><br>Sookie's lover Eric Northman, and his 'child' Pam are plotting something in secret. Whatever it is, they seem determined to keep Sookie out of it; almost as determined as Sookie is to find out what's going on. She can't sit on the sidelines when both her work and her love life are under threat - but as their plans gradually become clear Sookie finds the situation is deadlier than she could ever have imagined.<br><br><b>My Review</b>: Sookie Stackhouse's latest print outing. I'm sure I missed something along the way. Too many givens aren't what my memory offers...well, who knows, I might just be sufferin' from worsening Half-heimer's. It certainly feels that way when one is internetless for long stretches! Facts I gave not a second's thought to, because I could pop online and look 'em up, are all wetware storage reliant. I suspect the little elf who does my mental filing has grown very lazy in these internetty years.<br><br>Our various dramatis personae are all a-whirl in this outing...how odd, right?...over the Nevada vampire king, Felipe, choosing the reprehensible (even for a vampire) Victor as his Regent. Victor's got his knickers in a knot because he felt he should be King of Louisiana, not just Regent. And, insult to injury, Felipe is separating the Louisiana/Arkansas merger that was effected before the mass deaths two (possibly three) books ago when Sophie-Anne married whatever the King of Arkansas's name was before everyone at the wedding was slaughtered. Felipe chose to keep Eric, Sookie's vampire-rite husband, as Sheriff, the only individual so favored, and thus Victor's gunning (literally and figuratively) for him. Eric, Sookie, and some oddly assorted allies decide that gunnin' for someone is a two-way street after Victor is revealed as the force behind the new vamp club ruining Eric's business, and the roadhouse ruining Sam's beloved Merlotte's, in an unsubtle effort to make Eric come for Victor so Eric can be killed without explanation or expiation.<br><br>Yeah, good luck with that. And good luck to Eric in his new, unexpected, and possibly Sookie-less life, as arranged by his now-dead maker, very different from the one he has in <i>True Blood</i>.<br><br>Anyhoo, throw in Claude the hot gay faery/stripper, Dermot the damaged faery uncle, Mr. Cataliades the demon (literally not pejoratively) lawyer, Amelia the renegade witch and her former pussycat Bob, and a return visit from nutball Sandra Pelt, and the corpses stack up to agreeable heights in the accustomed way of Harris's books. As is expected in this series, the ending is another sea-change in the life of the Sookster, not yet brought quite to fruition. If this technique has palled on you, avoid this book.Well, what can one say? I mentioned in the last review that I wasn't at all ready to give up on bookish Bon Temps. This book does nothing to push me in one direction or the other. I liked it, and I was very pleased as always to immerse myself in the supe-filled universe that Sookie inhabits. I suspect that, barring a return to the terrible flatness of the un-fun <i>All Together Dead</i>, I'll read along in the series. I won't be out trolling for converts, though, like I do with Louise Penny's addictive-as-chocolate-coated-nicotine-infused-heroin-enrobed-crack Three Pines mysteries. I don't imagine my non-proselytic stance will harm Mother Harris's rep or bottom line.<br><br>I'll have to loop back and fill in some details from the book I missed. I suspect I've got the gist from Harris's carefully crafted fill-ins, but some of the fill-ins have left me curious about the full version. (Good job, Mother Harris! I'm tough to inveigle!)<br><br>And I am amused to note that <i>The Sookie Stackhouse Companion</i> is now available. Really? A concordance? How Biblical. I might not like Sookie's Jesusy thoughts, but isn't this a bit much?<br><br><a href="http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc-sa/3.0/deed.en_US" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img alt="Creative Commons License" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380148217i/680962.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>This work is licensed under a <a href="http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc-sa/3.0/deed.en_US" rel="nofollow noopener">Creative Commons Attribution-NonCommercial-ShareAlike 3.0 Unported License</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13027048693711963884" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_132690925" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132690925" />
    <a title="Yui" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3980858-yui"><img alt="Yui" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1278603460p2/3980858.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/132690925?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yui" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yui" href="/user/show/3980858-yui">Yui</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer132690925" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16481800648234161292"> <i>
  <b>3.5</b>
</i> <br/><br/>It's very tempting to give <i>
  <b>Dead Reckoning</b>
</i> 3stars because I feel it inferior in some ways to past Sookie Stackhouse novels but It isn't fair to grade a book just because I am holding a grudge to events that hasn't even happened in the book yet. <br/><br/>So for years of adoration and sheer insanity it stays with 4 stars on first glance ;)<br/><br/><br/> <b>WARNING!</b><br/><br/> <i>The following may contain spoilers.</i> <br/><br/><br/>Let me just get this quote out of my mind for it's been bugging me ever since I started reading DR.<br/><br/><i>...I suffered</i></span>
  <span id="freeText16481800648234161292" style="display:none"> <i>
  <b>3.5</b>
</i> <br /><br />It's very tempting to give <i>
  <b>Dead Reckoning</b>
</i> 3stars because I feel it inferior in some ways to past Sookie Stackhouse novels but It isn't fair to grade a book just because I am holding a grudge to events that hasn't even happened in the book yet. <br /><br />So for years of adoration and sheer insanity it stays with 4 stars on first glance ;)<br /><br /><br /> <b>WARNING!</b><br /><br /> <i>The following may contain spoilers.</i> <br /><br /><br />Let me just get this quote out of my mind for it's been bugging me ever since I started reading DR.<br /><br /><i>...I suffered with you, I hurt with you. I bled with you-not only because we're bonded, but because of the love I have for you.</i><br /><br />This was spoken by Eric in Dead in the Family. It keeps playing in the back of my mind while and after I read this. It is probably one of the stalest lines I have ever read but I remember the first time I read it in the back of Dead And Gone as a special preview while Sookie's torture is still fresh, I didn't find it corny or flat. It was one of the most emotional moments for me in the series. And even now I still feel more emotion than the actual written words. It served me as a charm throughout this book. <br /><br />The story in this book is divided in two parts. <br /><br />First is the attempt on Sookie's life. I admit I was satisfied and can classify this as a mystery worthy of Sookie Stackhouse but the perpetrator is an old character and is solved halfway thru the book.<br /><br />The second is the threat of Victor. I wasn't satisfied with this one because they have been dancing with him for 4 books now and they still ended up fighting him face to face. They have planned very carefully and in the end it seemed like the sufferings they endured and the time waiting was wasted since they defeated him easily. They even brought two new characters to plan and help but they ended up being useless. One of the characters I like who has a grudge with Victor is Heidi. She is talented and her story is very interesting. Her son was being held like a hostage to ensure her loyalty to Victor and it's a very good angle to work with but her worth was wasted because they focused on the other human who has no special traits and other contribution to offer.<br /><br />It really wasn't a bad read all in all. The writing is good. The story is good. I probably won't be complaining if it's my first C. Harris novel but since I've been following the series for years, it didn't meet my expectations. It might as well have ended up with a big cliff hanger since there have been new mysteries introduced like Sookie's real grandfather Fintan and a new threat to Sookie in life and in matters of the heart but both were left hanging. <br /><br />I feel instead of going forward, the story is going backward. Sookie started second guessing her self and her relationship with Eric isn't going forward.<br />They're married and they share a bond that lets them feel each others emotion but they still don't know each other well. They should have matured in their relationship by now but they are like a new couple on their 3rd date. The endearments Sookie's using <i>honey, honeybun?</i> makes me wince and have goose bumps. Instead of being sweet I feel like it's a sarcasm and been having bad premonitions. *sigh* I didn't feel the passion and warmth Eric used to make me feel whenever he said <i>"My lover"</i>.<br />Even the supporting characters are backtracking. Bill's back to throwing hints at Sookie which he should not be doing since Sookie's married already in vampire law with his sheriff no less! And everyone has a secret agenda and needs something from Sookie. It's like after years of struggling and coming out with friends in life threatening situations you should have been able to identify by now if not who your enemy is at least who your allies are. But no. It's like the past life savings didn't matter. Every body's plotting.<br /><br />Maybe Harris should wrap this series up and start another one instead of planning another 10 books with this. After 10years she still couldn't commit how many Sookie Stackhouse novels she's planning to write. I always thought this is a good thing because every SS books is long well written story and always bring something new. <br /><br />It's probably not Harris' fault that she spoiled us with the complex plots and many different treats before that the last 2 books feels like an anthology compare to the past 9 books. <br /><br />Maybe I'm just angry because I've been waiting for years for this Victor showdown and in the anticipation I didn't mind how much the price of this book is higher than the previous ones. I thought it's ok since the series has become quite popular and a lot of crappy novels are popping out and I sometimes find it insulting when a crappy book is priced higher than the really good ones but now I think the pricing is absurd. It is still worth a buy and even if a friend lend me a copy I will still pay to get my own definitely. But I could have waited for the original price to go down first...</span>
  <a data-text-id="16481800648234161292" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText5240465400520645323" style="display:none">Ok, I'm pissed. I really enjoyed the series up until this point and I really feel like this was simply a contractual obligation. There were some parts that were completely boring and hard to get through. There is so much double talk and all around the subject, that i couldn't get into it. Hell, from the first few pages I noticed that Sookie's voice was changed and it was not in a good way.<br /><br />What happened? <br /><br /><br />The things about the characters that we all grew to love (even if they were evil and unjust) all changed. Alcide (leader of the pack) doing what a fairy and a witch tell him? Who are these people? I want my 12.99 back plus the week it took me to get through this. NOW, i will never know what happens to Sookie because I probably won't read the next book. For shame.<br /><br /><br />I'm going to go back and read the first book and pretend like none of this happened.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10963731678602180988">Well I was anxiously awaiting the release of this book, hoping it would redeem the series for me after the last one. <br/><br/>Well I regret to say it didn't. Yes, it was better than the last one but it still left me dissatisfied. I'm not sure if it's me who has lost interest in the series or the author (but if you ask me her heart just isn't in it anymore). <br/><br/>I miss the bad ass Eric from the earlier books and wish he would come back. I'm tired of all the Sookie drama (seriously how much trouble can one per</span>
  <span id="freeText10963731678602180988" style="display:none">Well I was anxiously awaiting the release of this book, hoping it would redeem the series for me after the last one. <br /><br />Well I regret to say it didn't. Yes, it was better than the last one but it still left me dissatisfied. I'm not sure if it's me who has lost interest in the series or the author (but if you ask me her heart just isn't in it anymore). <br /><br />I miss the bad ass Eric from the earlier books and wish he would come back. I'm tired of all the Sookie drama (seriously how much trouble can one person get into) and I'm over the whole love triangle thing already.<br /><br />So I guess there it is. The book was just ok. At least it was better than the last one but was it good enough to keep me invested in any future books? I really don't think so, I may have to lay the Sookie Stackhouse series to rest.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_167356154" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167356154" />
    <a title="Sue Herbert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5419377-sue-herbert"><img alt="Sue Herbert" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167356154?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sue Herbert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sue Herbert" href="/user/show/5419377-sue-herbert">Sue Herbert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167356154" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7327769542090236837">Sookie, Sookie, Sookie. Will you make up your mind whether you like vampires or not? <br/><br/>I begin to think Sookie Stackhouse is actually not that nice a person. Perhaps I have over exposed myself, having ploughed my way through all the novels so far in short order, but there are elements on Dead Reckoning which feel awfully contrived. If you were being pursued by people in the rain and wanted to hide in a house, would you think of taking off ALL your clothes and dumping them in a bush? I mean how muc</span>
  <span id="freeText7327769542090236837" style="display:none">Sookie, Sookie, Sookie. Will you make up your mind whether you like vampires or not? <br /><br />I begin to think Sookie Stackhouse is actually not that nice a person. Perhaps I have over exposed myself, having ploughed my way through all the novels so far in short order, but there are elements on Dead Reckoning which feel awfully contrived. If you were being pursued by people in the rain and wanted to hide in a house, would you think of taking off ALL your clothes and dumping them in a bush? I mean how much do damp bra and knickers drip? Nope, not convinced, I felt that was a contrivance to create a situation, for no good reason that I could see other than to satisfy a particular fan base. I heard an interview with Ms Harris and even she could not really explain the reason for this episode. <br /><br />Then there is a Eric situation. I felt the books had what is now known as a 'story arch' in which Sookie was led, despite herself, towards Eric and he, despite himself, to her. This was all rather satisfying. Except that it now appears we may have peaked too soon, come to a climax prematurely and we're now heading downhill toward another conclusion altogether. Which can surely only be an anti climax, especially if Sookie does decide ultimately that what she wants is a nice domestic life, iced tea on the porch and someone to share it with. Looks to me as if she could end up with Sam after all at this rate. I have nothing against Sam, I'd just hoped for something more dramatic as a conclusion after what will be apparently be 13 books in all. Not to mention all that death, blood and destruction (which Sookie now appears to think she dislikes, despite having been co-instigator of the most recent bout)<br /><br />Sookie's attitude to her vampire lovers is inconsistent. She complains that Eric is scary and violent, yet dear lovely Bill kills three humans in defence of Sookie (one of them a relation) in the first book and this is never brought up against him. She complains that Eric is excited by violence and death, but she forgave Bill for having exactly the same reaction after the Dallas incident, when the Church of the New Sun attached the vampires and Bill ran off in pursuit instead of making sure Sookie was OK. She knows full well the fealty a vampire owes to his maker, it led to her break up with Bill, but when the full implications of this hit home, she's somewhat grumpy about it. She never has any consideration for the feelings of the men in her life, it's all about how what they do affects her. Does she really love any of them, or does she just enjoy the sex? <br /><br />I was left feeling that this book is setting us up for a conclusion I am possibly not going to like. I'll read the books anyway, they are a light, easy read and often very enjoyable. I thought I liked Sookie Stackhouse, but the selfishness she is starting to exhibit grates somewhat at the end of Dead Reckoning. Maybe she has to get selfish to protect herself, but the violent world she lives and loves in, was very much of her choosing. I guess if I become depressed I can always go back and read 'Dead to the World' again. Eric fan? Me? How did you guess? </span>
  <a data-text-id="7327769542090236837" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_167455768" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167455768" />
    <a title="Lighthearted" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1132923-lighthearted"><img alt="Lighthearted" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372874200p2/1132923.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/167455768?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lighthearted" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lighthearted" href="/user/show/1132923-lighthearted">Lighthearted</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1132923-lighthearted?shelf=supernatural-fiction">supernatural-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer167455768&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer167455768" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2126250055785688739">What is happening to the Sookie Stackhouse series??? At best, the characters were wooden; on occasion, they ventured into poor caricatures of themselves; at the worst, they weren’t even recognizable. In what universe would southern gentleman Bill tell Sookie she has great tits? As he’s declaring his love for her? Ack!<br/><br/>As the book continued, it became more and more ridiculous. At one point Sookie is being chased through the woods by an unknown number of assailants—she reaches Bill’s house but beca</span>
  <span id="freeText2126250055785688739" style="display:none">What is happening to the Sookie Stackhouse series??? At best, the characters were wooden; on occasion, they ventured into poor caricatures of themselves; at the worst, they weren’t even recognizable. In what universe would southern gentleman Bill tell Sookie she has great tits? As he’s declaring his love for her? Ack!<br /><br />As the book continued, it became more and more ridiculous. At one point Sookie is being chased through the woods by an unknown number of assailants—she reaches Bill’s house but because she doesn’t want the assailants to know which direction she went, she takes the time to take off her shoes and clothes, hide them behind bushes, and then wring out her hair so that they won’t be able to follow her drip marks. Really? She also forgets to lock the door behind her. Sure. Bill’s house is the obvious place to run but take off your clothes so they can’t really be certain that you’re there–and then neglect to lock the door. Uh huh. And I’m sorry but having run through a thunderstorm, no amount of hair-wringing is going to leave you drip-free without a towel. If Harris wanted Sookie naked in front of Bill, she should have worked harder to create a more believable scenario. To make a bad scenario worse, instead of thinking “holy crap, I’m trapped in a house, I don’t know who’s after me or why, holy crap!”, Sookie’s thoughts run from “dang it, here I go running to a man for help” to “silly men and their erections—okay, so what if I’m straddling him naked, people are after me” to “those selfish bastards, who do they think they are, leaving all of the lights on in Bill’s house”. Seriously??? And when the bad guys are gone and Bill’s awake, he doesn’t offer to lend her a shirt, pajamas, anything? He gets dressed and she keeps traipsing around in a shawl/tablecloth with an apparently open-weave???<br /><br />The fight scene at Fangtasia was nearly as bad. A vampire’s arm gets lopped off and she makes the best of it by whacking someone else with it? Was I supposed to laugh at this? And Eric may have his selfish tendencies but unless the previous books were a lie, he loves Sookie and would not have chomped on her neck like that, even angry. Speaking of Eric, the sex scene earlier in the book was just wrong—one, it’s not sexy when the characters have as little of an emotional connection as these two do in this book and two, it’s not sexy if you need to place an icepack on your “yahoo place” afterwards.<br /><br />There were so many things I hated about this book that I can’t remember if there was any aspect of it I liked. The only reason that I continued reading is because I’m such a fan of the series—I’m hoping Harris rediscovers her love of the story before she writes the next book and I want to be prepared to read it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2126250055785688739" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11884878028501593981"><b>2019 Re-Read</b><br/><br/>You can get whiplash trying to keep up with Sookie Stackhouse’s life—one day you’re planning a vampire assassination, the next it’s a mundane baby shower. One evening you hand out sharpened stakes, the next cake and napkins.<br/><br/>This is the volume of the series where Sookie realizes how much her life has changed—how much she has changed.   <span id="freeText11884878028501593981" style="display:none"><b>2019 Re-Read</b><br /><br />You can get whiplash trying to keep up with Sookie Stackhouse’s life—one day you’re planning a vampire assassination, the next it’s a mundane baby shower. One evening you hand out sharpened stakes, the next cake and napkins.<br /><br />This is the volume of the series where Sookie realizes how much her life has changed—how much she has changed. For several books now, Sookie has noted that she’s a “bad Christian.” Now she knows where her telepathic talent comes from (an indiscretion of her grandmother’s) and her world has expanded to include all sorts of supernatural creatures. She has left behind her “nice girl next door” persona and is becoming a woman to be conjured with.<br /><br />It’s inevitable that this will change her relationship with Eric, who is used to being the vampire in charge. He’s getting surly and pouty, not liking this change in his ‘wife.’ She’s standing up for herself and for others, something that controlling spouses find disconcerting.<br /><br />I amazed, actually, at how many human relationship issues that Harris manages to tackle through this urban fantasy soap-opera. As Sookie learns more about herself and managing her feelings &amp; expectations, we all get to review these life lessons through her interior monologue. How often women are expected to ‘be nice’ and acquiesce to the demands of men, plus how they get labelled as bitches when they don’t follow this script.<br /><br />Still loving Pam, still carrying a torch for Bill, really appreciating Bubba. <br /><br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16664780949629989886">It's a very sad day for me when I have to give Miss Stackhouse an average 3 star rating. I missed being in Sookie's world, but not so much that I enjoyed trailing along with her while she cleaned her home, picked up breakfast, pumped her gas, showered, shaved her legs, or washed dirty dishes. I understand Sookie is one of the more ordinary characters - to an extent- in a world that has become abundant in supernaturals, but I was desperately wishing for more action on numerous occassions. <br/><br/><br/>*******</span>
  <span id="freeText16664780949629989886" style="display:none">It's a very sad day for me when I have to give Miss Stackhouse an average 3 star rating. I missed being in Sookie's world, but not so much that I enjoyed trailing along with her while she cleaned her home, picked up breakfast, pumped her gas, showered, shaved her legs, or washed dirty dishes. I understand Sookie is one of the more ordinary characters - to an extent- in a world that has become abundant in supernaturals, but I was desperately wishing for more action on numerous occassions. <br /><br /><br />******* Warning!!! May contain a few light spoilers*******<br /><br />I wasn't very pleased with the amount or the quality of Sookie and Eric time. It was less than satisfying, and not just because of the major obstacle that was revealed.<br /><br />I didn't find the predicament with <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Sandra Pelt <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> intense or suspenseful. I realize she was maniacal and dangerous, but she was also something else . . . worn-out and uninteresting. <br /><br />Also, it would have been nice if we were actually able to get to know a little more about Miriam. The circumstances were unfortunate, but since I knew almost nothing about her, it was difficult to stir up any strong emotions with the direction that particular situation went in. <br /><br />This is where I would mention the ordeal with Alcide, but I'm not going to because I've recently decided that it's too absurb to acknowledge.<br /><br />Then there were other problems I had that I suppose would be considered more trivial.<br /><br />For example, Eric's new daytime man - a person who should, at the very least, be trustworthy. Eric has never come across as an individual who would tolerate a daytime man that he described as having "plenty of attitude" and shows an open dislike toward vampires. He was highly recommended by Bubba and hates Victor and that was enough for Eric? That situation just struck me as odd and uncharacteristic.<br /><br />Then there was Terry being a "spy" against Sookie for Eric and Niall. Sookie has always liked Terry and they've always been cordial, but it's not like she's ever spilled secrets to him or has been close to him at all. Again, that was just odd to me.<br /><br />There was also the trip to the elementary school. I thought there was a greater purpose there or that it would tie into something else. I was wrong. It was just a reason to remind us of Sookie's obligations toward Hunter, I suppose.<br /><br />This isn't the entire list, but I see no reason to continue to complain when I have other new releases waiting on me. ;) So I guess I will end this with . . . <br /><br />Better luck next time?</span>

<div id="review_166022472" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166022472" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2158779-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1237953080p2/2158779.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/166022472?book_show_action=true">May 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/2158779-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10763935-dead-reckoning">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2158779-ashley?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2158779-ashley?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2158779-ashley?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166022472" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7668152937430967735">I waited a year, telling myself that the worrisome feeling I was left with after Dead in the Family was a one-off sensation. I told myself "she'll get back in her groove with Dead Reckoning." I had it delivered to my Kindle so I didn't even have to fight with book-store staff on release day. I wanted so very, very badly for this book to be a return to the Sookie Stackhouse books of the early series.<br/><br/>I wish I could say it met my expectations and then blew me away. But I'd be lying.<br/><br/>It's not a BAD b</span>
  <span id="freeText7668152937430967735" style="display:none">I waited a year, telling myself that the worrisome feeling I was left with after Dead in the Family was a one-off sensation. I told myself "she'll get back in her groove with Dead Reckoning." I had it delivered to my Kindle so I didn't even have to fight with book-store staff on release day. I wanted so very, very badly for this book to be a return to the Sookie Stackhouse books of the early series.<br /><br />I wish I could say it met my expectations and then blew me away. But I'd be lying.<br /><br />It's not a BAD book, I'll start there. The dialogue is left wanting, and she recycles a few very key metaphors throughout the story, but her writing wasn't my main complaint. It DID lack the beautiful tension that Charlaine Harris has delivered in the past, and that more than anything was what disappointed me.<br /><br />Dead Reckoning, much like Dead in the Family, feels like filler. In Dead Reckoning I felt as if Harris had gone through the FAQ section of a Sookie fan page and decided to answer a bunch of arbitrary questions, like "can Sam breed in dog form" and "what happened with Amelia and Bob." And man, oh, man the secondary characters are crammed into this book in force. From Eric's vampire posse, to Amelia and Bob, to the Merlotte's staff, to Bubba and Alcide. Not many get left behind, but all the interactions felt rushed. The back story with Sookie's grandmother fell flat, and I didn't really buy into the relationship with Sookie and her fairy-kin.<br /><br />And then there was Sookie and Eric. I longed for this couple. PINED for this couple. By the time book 4 rolled around I thought I might combust over the tension. But between this book and the last, they've lost me. Their dialogue was weak and Eric, to be frank, was kind of a turd. And not just in the "I'm a very old vampire who has important things to do" way. No. He was just an overbearing, pushy, domineering jerk. And suddenly Bill is back in her life, acting like he's a viable option? Am I the only one who remembered how betrayed she felt?<br /><br />The general feeling I got from the book was that Harris tried to introduce way too much but did too little with it. I wasn't really pulled into the book until almost 40% in when the good old stand-by "crazy Sandra Pelt" plot was brought in. The book would have been sensational if it was Sookie and the Leeds's trying to fend off Sandra while Eric and the vamps dealt with Victor.<br /><br />Guess I'll be waiting another year to see if she can bring it back around. I'm sad to say it, but I just want it to end. The series has lost its magic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7668152937430967735" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review166022472">

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hVx9rzaNIbCsJOcHW2PT5ORHHKI3PuBlfNEloBNT6ieYfz9bHI1xeWbRaUDQ76e7Dq/r6HuJg3rt+08WIpAhag==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BceZXjNBxF5VYyoJz0cNSrEKOr088EZkPQgHEm9TqTUY5NuqGUGUl5+WpE5Ey3kVW+LN93BHJXusIm2kXpBieA==')})
  }
//]]>

Pickett ministered to 95 men before they were put to death by lethal injection. They came with sinister nicknames like &quot;The Candy Man&quot; and &quot;The Good Samaritan Killer,&quot; some contrite, some angry-a few who might even have been innocent. All of them found in Rev. This first-hand experience gave Rev. Pickett the unique insight needed to write an impassioned statement on the realities of capital punishment in America.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/17061.Charlaine_Harris">About Charlaine Harris</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer639925146159874329">Charlaine Harris has been a published novelist for over thirty-five years. A native of the Mississippi Delta, she grew up in the middle of a cotton field. Charlaine lives in Texas now, and all of her children and grandchildren are within easy driving distance.<br/><br/>Though her early output consisted largely of ghost stories, by the time she hit college (Rhodes, in Memphis) Charlaine was writing poetry an</span>
  <span id="freeText639925146159874329" style="display:none">Charlaine Harris has been a published novelist for over thirty-five years. A native of the Mississippi Delta, she grew up in the middle of a cotton field. Charlaine lives in Texas now, and all of her children and grandchildren are within easy driving distance.<br /><br />Though her early output consisted largely of ghost stories, by the time she hit college (Rhodes, in Memphis) Charlaine was writing poetry and plays. After holding down some low-level jobs, her husband Hal gave her the opportunity to stay home and write. The resulting two stand-alones were published by Houghton Mifflin. After a child-producing sabbatical, Charlaine latched on to the trend of series, and soon had her own traditional mystery books about a Georgia librarian, Aurora Teagarden. Her first Teagarden, <i>Real Murders</i>, garnered an Agatha nomination.<br /><br />Soon Charlaine was looking for another challenge, and the result was the much darker Lily Bard series. The books, set in Shakespeare, Arkansas, feature a heroine who has survived a terrible attack and is learning to live with its consequences. <br /><br />When Charlaine began to realize that neither of those series was ever going to set the literary world on fire, she regrouped and decided to write the book she’d always wanted to write. Not a traditional mystery, nor yet pure science fiction or romance, <i>Dead Until Dark</i> broke genre boundaries to appeal to a wide audience of people who simply enjoy a good adventure. Each subsequent book about Sookie Stackhouse, telepathic Louisiana barmaid and friend to vampires, werewolves, and various other odd creatures, was very successful in many languages.<br /><br />The Harper Connelly books were written concurrently with the Sookie novels. <br /><br />Following the end of Sookie's recorded adventures, Charlaine wrote the "Midnight, Texas" books, which have become a television series, also. The Aurora Teagarden books have been adapted by Hallmark Movie &amp; Mystery.<br /><br />Charlaine is a member of many professional organizations, an Episcopalian, and currently the lucky houseparent to two rescue dogs. She lives on a cliff overlooking the Brazos River.</span>
  <a data-text-id="639925146159874329" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
